<div class=\"widget widget-ArticleFulltext widget-instance-OUP_Article_FullText_Widget\">\n        <div class=\"module-widget\">\r\n    <div class=\"widget-items\" data-widgetname=\"ArticleFulltext\">\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n                    <h2 scrollto-destination=45586457 id=\"45586457\" class=\"abstract-title\" >Abstract</h2>\r\n<section class=\"abstract\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">We report the discovery of an optical Einstein ring in the Sculptor constellation, IAC J010127-334319, in the vicinity of the Sculptor dwarf spheroidal galaxy. It is an almost complete ring (\u223c300\u00b0) with a diameter of\u00a0\u223c4.5\u2009arcsec. The discovery was made serendipitously from inspecting Dark Energy Camera (DECam) archive imaging data. Confirmation of the object nature has been obtained by deriving spectroscopic redshifts for both components, lens and source, from observations at the 10.4\u00a0m Gran Telescopio CANARIAS (GTC) with the spectrograph OSIRIS. The lens, a massive early-type galaxy, has a redshift of <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.581, while the source is a starburst galaxy with redshift of <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.165. The total enclosed mass that produces the lensing effect has been estimated to be <em>M</em><sub>tot</sub>\u00a0=\u00a0(1.86 \u00b1 0.23)\u2009\u00d7\u200910<sup>12</sup>\u2009M<sub>\u2299</sub>.</p></section>                        <div class=\"article-metadata-panel clearfix\"></div>\r\n<div class=\"kwd-group\"><a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;gravitational lensing: strong&quot;\">gravitational lensing: strong</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;galaxies: distances and redshifts&quot;\">galaxies: distances and redshifts</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;galaxies: elliptical and lenticular, cD&quot;\">galaxies: elliptical and lenticular, cD</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;galaxies: evolution&quot;\">galaxies: evolution</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;galaxies: starburst&quot;\">galaxies: starburst</a></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=45586461 id=\"45586461\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec1>1 INTRODUCTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Strongly lensed galaxies are very important in the study of galaxy formation and evolution because they permit derivation of important physical parameters such as the total mass of the lensing object, without any assumption on the dynamics. Cases in which the Einstein ring (ER) is almost complete and the central lensing galaxy isolated are rare; these permit constraining with great accuracy the enclosed mass within the projected Einstein radius \u0398<sub>E</sub> (Kochanek, Keeton &amp; McLeod <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2001</a>). Miralda-Escud\u00e9 &amp; Leh\u00e1r (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1992</a>) predicted several 10<sup>6</sup> optical ER to be detectable over the whole sky, down to a magnitude limit of <em>B</em>\u00a0=\u00a026 and a lower limit for the enclosed mass of <em>M</em>\u00a0\u223c 5\u2009\u00d7\u200910<sup>11</sup>\u2009M<sub>\u2299</sub>. This notwithstanding, despite extensive surveys (see for example Bolton et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>; Stark et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>) only a few tens of complete or nearly complete optical ERs have been identified so far, and among these objects, only a few show a close similarity, in morphology and elongation of the ring, to the one we discuss in this present work.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The first ER to be discovered is the radio source MG1131+0456 (Hewitt et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib10\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib10\" data-open=\"bib10\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1988</a>). Warren et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1996</a>) report the discovery of a partial ER (\u223c170\u00b0) with \u0398<sub>E</sub>\u00a0\u223c 1.35\u2009arcsec; the background O<span class=\"small-caps\">\u00a0ii</span> emitting galaxy at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a03.595 is lensed by an elliptical massive galaxy at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.485. This is the first known case in the literature of an ER discovered at optical wavelengths. Cabanac et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2005</a>) discovered an almost complete ER (\u223c260\u00b0) with \u0398<sub>E</sub>\u00a0\u223c 1.48\u2009arcsec produced by a massive and isolated elliptical galaxy at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.986. The source galaxy is a starburst at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a03.773. Then, a similar ER to the one we report in this Letter, in morphology, but not in the physics of the source galaxy, a BX galaxy, is the so called Cosmic Horseshoe (Belokurov et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib2\" data-open=\"bib2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>); the ring extension is similar to the one we report here, (\u223c300\u00b0), but the Einstein radius is double, \u0398<sub>E</sub>\u00a0\u223c 5\u2009arcsec; the lensing galaxy has a huge mass of\u00a0\u223c<em>M</em>\u00a0=\u00a05.4\u2009\u00d7 10<sup>12</sup>\u2009M<sub>\u2299</sub>. Other partial ER discovered recently are: the \u2018Cosmic Eye\u2019 (Smail et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib21\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib21\" data-open=\"bib21\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>), the \u20188 o'clock arc\u2019 (Allam et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>) and the \u2018Clone\u2019 (Lin et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib15\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib15\" data-open=\"bib15\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Here, we report the discovery of IAC J010127-334319, an optical, almost complete ER, that we refer to as the \u2018Canarias Einstein Ring\u2019, noticed as a peculiar object in DECam images. No previous reference to the object has been found in the literature. Subsequently, we observed it with OSIRIS@GTC for a spectroscopic confirmation of its nature. In this Letter, we provide the first physical parameters of this system. In the following discussion, we assume that a flat cosmology with \u03a9<sub>m</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.3, \u03a9<sub>\u039b</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.7 and <em>H</em><sub>0</sub>\u00a0=\u00a070\u2009km\u2009s<sup>\u22121</sup>\u2009Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup>.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=45586467 id=\"45586467\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2>2 DISCOVERY</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The serendipitous discovery of IAC J010127-334319 was made, while performing photometry on stacked images, in <em>g</em> and <em>r</em> filters, taken with DECam (Flaugher et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib9\" data-open=\"bib9\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) at the Blanco 4\u00a0m telescope at the Cerro Tololo Inter-American Observatory (CTIO), reduced with the NOAO Community Pipeline (Valdes et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>) and obtained from the NOAO Science Archive (Seaman et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>). The total exposure time is 7680\u00a0s in the <em>g</em> filter and 5700\u00a0s in the <em>r</em> filter. Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a> shows the resulting colour composite image: it is evident that two components with different colours are present. In particular, the central one (the lens) appears redder than the second component (the lensed image of the source), which in turn appears as elongated all around the first. The ring is almost perfectly circular with an apparent radius of 8\u2009px which translates to 2.16\u2009arcsec. Three peaks, A, B and C, are clearly visible (bottom-right panel of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>); they are located respectively at \u2212150\u00b0, 14\u00b0 and 83\u00b0 from North counterclockwise. In Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>, all the derived parameters for the object are listed. From the DECam photometry, we estimated an apparent magnitude for the lens in both <em>g</em> and <em>r</em> bands of <em>g</em>\u00a0=\u00a023.61 and <em>r</em>\u00a0=\u00a021.40. The colour (<em>g</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>r</em>)\u00a0&gt;\u00a02 indicates that this galaxy is probably a luminous red galaxy (Eisenstein et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib8\" data-open=\"bib8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2001</a>). All the details about the photometric calibration will be given in a forthcoming paper (Bettinelli et\u00a0al., in preparation).</p>                        <a id=\"45586469\" (mag\u2009arcsec<sup>\u22122</sup>):\u00a0</td><td>23.9,\u200923.2\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>Surface brightness C (<em>g,r</em>) (mag\u2009arcsec<sup>\u22122</sup>):\u00a0</td><td>23.7,\u200923.0\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>Apparent magnitude (<em>g,r</em>)\u00a0</td><td>20.94,\u200920.12\u00a0</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div       </a></div></div></div><div class=\"table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl1\" data-id=\"tbl1\"><span class=\"label\">Table (<em>g,r</em>)\u00a0</td><td>\u221221.05, \u221223.18\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>Ring\u00a0</td><td>\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>Redshift:\u00a0</td><td>1.165 \u00b1 0.001\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>Einstein (mag\u2009arcsec<sup>\u22122</sup>):\u00a0</td><td>23.9,\u200923.2\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>Surface brightness C (<em>g,r</em>) (mag\u2009arcsec<sup>\u22122</sup>):\u00a0</td><td>23.7,\u200923.0\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>Apparent magnitude (<em>g,r</em>)\u00a0</td><td>20.94,\u200920.12\u00a0</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/45586470\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=45586471 id=\"45586471\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3>3 FOLLOW-UP SPECTROSCOPY</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">In order to confirm the lensing nature of this system, we performed a spectroscopic follow-up at the 10.4\u00a0m Gran Telescopio CANARIAS (GTC) on Roque de los Muchachos Observatory (La Palma, Spain) using the Optical System for Imaging and low-Intermediate-Resolution Integrated Spectroscopy (OSIRIS) spectrograph (Cepa <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib6\" data-open=\"bib6\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1998</a>). OSIRIS has a mosaic of two E2V CCD42-82 (2048\u00a0\u00d7\u00a04096\u2009px). All the obtained spectra were registered on the second detector, which is the default for long-slit spectroscopy. We used a binning of 2\u00a0\u00d7\u00a02 providing a pixel size of 0.254\u2009arcsec\u2009px<sup>\u22121</sup>, and the grism R300B, which provides a spectral coverage of 4000\u20139000\u00a0\u00c5 and a nominal dispersion of 4.96\u00a0\u00c5 px<sup>\u22121</sup>. The slit width was 0.6\u2009arcsec. Long-slit spectral observations were performed on 2015 December 2 in good seeing conditions of\u00a0\u223c0.8\u2009arcsec. The slit was placed along the N\u2013S direction, in order to minimize the effects of atmospheric differential refraction at culmination. The total exposure time was 3600\u00a0s divided into six exposures of 600\u00a0s each. In each of the six exposures, the two components, ring and lensing galaxy, have been detected and in particular their spectra were not overlapping. The position of the slit was such that the spectra obtained for the ring refers to peak B.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">For the pre-reduction, we have used the OSIRIS Offline Pipeline Software (<span class=\"small-caps\">oops</span>); sky subtraction and flux calibration were performed using <span class=\"small-caps\">iraf</span>.<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn1\" data-open=\"fn1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\"><sup>1</sup></a> We performed wavelength calibration using standard HgAr+Ne+Xe arc lamps; the resulting error on wavelength determination has been measured to be consistent with the above spectral resolution. We corrected the extracted spectra for instrumental response using observations of the spectrophotometric standard star GD140, a white dwarf, obtained the same night. The fluxes of this standard star are available in Massey et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib16\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib16\" data-open=\"bib16\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1988</a>).</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=45586474 id=\"45586474\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4>4 ANALYSIS AND DISCUSSION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">In order to derive the redshifts for the two components, we noted the strong emission line in the source spectrum and the 4000\u00a0\u00c5 Balmer discontinuity in the lens spectrum. This led us to choose template models for a starburst galaxy and an early-type galaxy, respectively, as specified below. Following line identification, we determined redshifts.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=45586476 id=\"45586476\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4-1>4.1 Lens</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Using the template spectra by Kinney et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1996</a>) results that the spectrum of the lens galaxy fits well the spectrum of a S0 galaxy (see Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>), a typical early-type galaxy characterized by a large increase in flux from the UV part of the spectrum to the optical. The 4000 \u00c5 Balmer discontinuity at\u00a0\u223c6330 \u00c5 is noticeable. The redshift of the lens galaxy is <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.581 \u00b1 0.001, and it has been determined from the measurements of: H\u03b7\u2009\u03bb3835.4, Ca K \u03bb3933.7, Ca H \u03bb3968.5, H\u03b4\u2009\u03bb4141.8, <em>G</em>-band \u03bb4307.7, Mg-b2 \u03bb5172.7, Mg-b1 \u03bb5183.6 (marked red features from left to right in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> middle panel).</p>                        <a id=\"45586478\" scrollto-destination=\"45586478\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig2\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 2.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnrasl/461/1/10.1093_mnrasl_slw097/2/m_slw097fig2.jpeg?Expires=1611467003&amp;Signature=dQ95PdNHSlylwjsDmP7ZBhQ7jP0QfJxvpjFLExWcWgnG1khTu6mKzPQTZ5y6eSBQxCblbQTYMHHd-MIBYMzZWKZLdC-AB3J2wxKJFIdvqekfaw18bjrfNTsPdmbZ6u6SlUrmf4gcS26pNOTbbiMZOKtaJIr3poMZGOVzvknriiNfQ8URtfs6AGnKlX6RmYJwpQ7s08qNyLXoyanpkUt7EDb98-2UIXdk13R4oSyO8juC19a6xB6MKUQjKGodSaKA4rXRIilZF02XlcotIOoMxJf2hthXSPWY9qdJJ-WlHswdjIKOcUd9MKGFRS1IJTNOpLF8Sv8fZuBbt7I8U0nT1Q__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Top panel: source galaxy spectrum (in blue) with overplotted a starburst template spectrum by Calzetti, Kinney &amp; Storchi-Bergmann (1994). Bottom panel: measured wavelength displacement between observed and laboratory line position for the selected features (see text for details).\" data-path-from-xml=\"slw097fig2.jpeg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/45586478/slw097fig2.jpeg\" data-path-from-xml=\"slw097fig2.jpeg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"45586478\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnrasl/461/1/10.1093_mnrasl_slw097/2/slw097fig2.jpeg?Expires=1611467003&Signature=N9KIUcpvedrF3zWgrjKyPcYgWg76dV5MFdX6auNQjRRnRTA9GUhxiBNClsHyvhkS4B49rdwqAzRGReNUv7NpnfO1qXv5wgbU05HoBbFhGUdXnrO7~LUjekLCm~LPc3Ftu08hO8zbZTJx7s-PNS3aD2XmvlNuynUKmTGQNPE2LpRLorN7Oi8ERSQIHDbMHG1ZRHAedk0a7v1waI~I7MGPURpk0aZ6XU8mPrdl9Ha~RRtGZvv10oJDK1M2vTOg~LmZk9oDRWsapa3mufthqdYP7J0I9HZ8LHtSHB6pTboCEN2zpAAQ1KLSN7d947kmGj-PbY3W-yaXJ2u1iNZahqPcyQ__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=45586478&ar=2589629&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5327\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"slw097fig2.jpeg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Top panel: source galaxy spectrum (in blue) with overplotted a starburst template spectrum by Calzetti, Kinney &amp; Storchi-Bergmann (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1994</a>). Middle panel: lens galaxy spectrum (in red) with overplotted an early-type galaxy template by Kinney et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1996</a>). Bottom panel: measured wavelength displacement between observed and laboratory line position for the selected features (see text for details).</p></div></div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=45586479 id=\"45586479\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4-2>4.2 Source</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">For the source galaxy, we used the template spectra by Calzetti et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1994</a>), and we found that the spectrum best fitting our observed spectrum corresponds to a starburst galaxy in the case of clumpy scattering slab, where it is assumed that clumped dust is located close to the source of radiation. In such circumstances, Calzetti et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1994</a>) show that scattering into the line of sight dominates over absorption by the dust, providing a significant positive contribution to the emerging radiation. This template spectrum fits well the strong O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> \u03bb3727 emission line. We also identified the following lines: Fe\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> \u03bb2344.0, Fe\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> \u03bb2600.0, H\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">i</span>\u00a011 \u03bb3770.6, O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> \u03bb3727.3, H\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">i</span>\u00a010 \u03bb3797.9 (marked blue features from left to right in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> upper panel). According to these features, we derived for the source galaxy a redshift of <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.165 \u00b1 0.001. We note that the selected slit position enable us to extract only the portion of the spectrum corresponding to peak B (see Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>); this notwithstanding, the O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> emission coming from the opposite side of the ring can be easily noted in our spectra.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=45586481 id=\"45586481\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4-3>4.3 Enclosed mass derivation</h3>\r\n<div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">The strong circular symmetry, of our object (see Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>), suggests that it can be approximated to the case of a circularly symmetric lens, with source and lens in the line of sight. Under these assumptions, for an arbitrary mass profile M(\u0398) (i.e. without assuming any particular model for the potential), we can apply the following relation (Narayan &amp; Bartelmann <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib19\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib19\" data-open=\"bib19\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1996</a>) and solve it for the mass. <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ1\" content-id=\"equ1\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{equation}\r\n\\Theta ^{2}_{\\rm E}\\, =\\, \\frac{4{\\rm G}}{\\rm c^{2}}\\, {\\rm M}(\\Theta )\\, \\frac{\\mathrm{d}_{\\rm LS}}{\\mathrm{d}_{\\rm L}d_{\\rm S}}\r\n\\end{equation} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(1)</span></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Here, \u0398<sub>E</sub> is the Einstein radius in radians; M(\u0398) is the mass enclosed within the Einstein radius; <em>d</em><sub>LS</sub>, <em>d</em><sub>L</sub>, <em>d</em><sub>S</sub> are the angular diameter distances, respectively, of source-lens, lens-observer and source-observer. These last quantities are related to the relative comoving distances and, in general, this relation depends on the assumed curvature of the Universe (Hogg <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1999</a>). In our case, \u03a9<sub>K</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00 has been assumed, and the resulting angular diameter distances are <em>d</em><sub>L</sub>\u00a0=\u00a0951\u2009h<sup>\u22121</sup> Mpc, <em>d</em><sub>S</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01192\u2009h<sup>\u22121</sup> Mpc and <em>d</em><sub>LS</sub>\u00a0=\u00a0498\u2009h<sup>\u22121</sup> Mpc. We calculated a total mass <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\rm M_{tot}=(1.86 \\pm 0.23) \\,\\times 10^{12}\\, {\\rm M_{{\\odot }}}}$|</span> where the error on the mass (12\u2009per\u2009cent) is overwhelmingly due to the measurement error in the determination of the Einstein radius, which we have estimated to be 0.5\u2009px which corresponds to 0.135\u2009arcsec. The error on the redshift derives from the error estimated on the wavelength calibration, which is\u00a0\u223c5\u00a0\u00c5. This value is consistent with the spectral resolution (4.96\u00a0\u00c5 px<sup>\u22121</sup>) of the grating R300B that we used.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Under the assumption of a singular isothermal sphere (SIS), it is possible to give an estimate of the magnification of the ring: \u03bc\u00a0=\u00a04\u0398<sub>E</sub>/\u03b4\u0398<sub>s</sub>, where \u03b4\u0398<sub>s</sub> is the source size. From Nagy et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>), the average size of a starburst galaxy in our redshift range is\u00a0\u223c2 Kpc, which corresponds to 0.24\u2009arcsec. The derived magnification is\u00a0\u223c36.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We determined also the mass-to-light ratio of the lens in the g band; a <em>K</em>-correction of 2.1 has been derived for the lens using the NED calculator (Chilingarian &amp; Zolotukhin <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>). The resulting ratio is M<sub>tot</sub>/L\u00a0\u223c 58\u2009M<sub>\u2299</sub>/L<sub>\u2299</sub>.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The former mass estimate can be improved by applying to the system a singular isothermal ellipsoid (SIE) model using the <span class=\"small-caps\">gravlens/lensmodel</span> software (Keeton <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2001</a>). This software allows to fit a SIE model using only the image positions and fluxes. The obtained best-fitting model is plotted in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>. The solutions have been derived for point-like sources; the ring shape is due to the fact that the source should actually be more extended with respect to the caustics than is shown here. The best fit ellipticity is 0.2 calculated as 1\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>q</em>, where <em>q</em> is the axis ratio; the associated position angle is \u221257\u00b0, angle measured from North to East. The best-fitting \u03c7<sup>2</sup> value is 6.12, calculated setting to 0 the weights relative to image fluxes. The derived Einstein radius is \u0398<sub>E</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.38\u2009arcsec, which translates in an enclosed mass of\u00a0\u223c2.26\u2009\u00d7\u200910<sup>12</sup>\u2009M<sub>\u2299</sub>, hence, in excellent agreement with our previous estimate.</p>                        <a id=\"45586487\" scrollto-destination=\"45586487\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig3\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 3.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnrasl/461/1/10.1093_mnrasl_slw097/2/m_slw097fig3.jpeg?Expires=1611467003&amp;Signature=aX8sMFyrc965mhtX4T7epk~b2N01eLX59zQHg69zxMYc7WAhExEZBIso5JO5yP4PCbOlDrF6Nze7U4jhZVrKgnrvTgQt2ydIFxRX9Ha20I4vb9lDuGR1VNeyhrz-wDvaFPcz0rBGYJYy0ruFkt~ia463J5m3SdDc04u8ySoyfE2cKuQ1QlCJoC15PGHukZ32JZevD9bWonAKAdxClYaRWimKtyPVZJfdjBQbMSnCkACptlUHCXtC4KOh3oCgqgzxoLKGzqp1JtVR7~5rDnSQ3OCVQOVH~tBOOU-27cGjC0Ftj42pLTaoyQ4sFufWXgq6IKC-I-77iwY9Z~gOL0zBww__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Best-fitting SIE model obtained with the gravlens/lensmodel software. On the left (image plane): the source images positions are plotted as blue triangles, the fitted position recovered by the software as blue squares, the red central dot represents the position of the lensing galaxy and the red curve is the critical curve. On the right (source plane): the blue square represents the calculated position of the source; the caustics are shown in red.</p></div></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=45586488 id=\"45586488\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5>5 CONCLUSIONS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We report the discovery of an almost complete (\u223c300\u00b0) circular optical ER in the constellation of Sculptor. The gravitational lens is a massive luminous red galaxy at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.581. The source galaxy is a starburst at redshift <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.165; its spectrum is dominated by a strong O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> emission line. Using these redshift determinations and the Einstein radius \u0398<sub>E</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.16\u2009arcsec, we calculated the total enclosed mass that produced the lensing effect: <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\rm M_{tot}=(1.86 \\pm 0.23) \\times 10^{12}\\, {\\rm M_{{\\odot }}}}$|\u2060</span>.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">All the parameters, we determined for IAC J010127-334319, are listed in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The authors thank the anonymous referee for the constructive comments that significantly improved the manuscript. The authors are grateful to all the GTC staff and in particular to Dr A. Cabrera-Lavers for his support in refining the spectroscopical observations during the Phase-2. The authors also thank Dr J. Falc\u00f3n-Barroso for the helpful discussion.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">This Letter is based on observations made with the GTC telescope, in the Spanish Observatorio del Roque de los Muchachos of the Instituto de Astrof\u00edsica de Canarias, under Director's Discretionary Time.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">This project used data obtained with theDECam, which was constructed by the Dark Energy Survey (DES) collaboration. Funding for the DES Projects has been provided by the DOE and NSF (USA), MISE (Spain), STFC (UK), HEFCE (UK), NCSA (UIUC), KICP (U. Chicago), CCAPP (Ohio State), MIFPA (Texas A&amp;M), CNPQ, FAPERJ, FINEP (Brazil), MINECO (Spain), DFG (Germany) and the collaborating institutions in the Dark Energy Survey, which are Argonne Lab, UC Santa Cruz, University of Cambridge, CIEMAT-Madrid, University of Chicago, University College London, DES-Brazil Consortium, University of Edinburgh, ETH Z\u00fcrich, Fermilab, University of Illinois, ICE (IEEC-CSIC), IFAE Barcelona, Lawrence Berkeley Lab, LMU M\u00fcnchen and the associated Excellence Cluster Universe, University of Michigan, NOAO, University of Nottingham, Ohio State University, University of Pennsylvania, University of Portsmouth, SLAC National Lab, Stanford University, University of Sussex and Texas A&amp;M University.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">MB, MS, AA, SLH, SC and GP acknowledge support from the Spanish Ministry of Economy and Competitiveness (MINECO) under grant AYA2013-42781.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">This research has made use of the NASA/IPAC Extragalactic Database (NED), which is operated by the Jet Propulsion Laboratory, California Institute of Technology, under contract with the National Aeronautics and Space Administration.</p><div <div class=\"widget widget-ArticleFulltext widget-instance-OUP_Article_FullText_Widget\">\n        <div class=\"module-widget\">\r\n    <div class=\"widget-items\" data-widgetname=\"ArticleFulltext\">\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n                    <h2 scrollto-destination=45586457 id=\"45586457\" class=\"abstract-title\" >Abstract</h2>\r\n<section class=\"abstract\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">We report the discovery of an optical Einstein ring in the Sculptor constellation, IAC J010127-334319, in the vicinity of the Sculptor dwarf spheroidal galaxy. It is an almost complete ring (\u223c300\u00b0) with a diameter of\u00a0\u223c4.5\u2009arcsec. The discovery was made serendipitously from inspecting Dark Energy Camera (DECam) archive imaging data. Confirmation of the object nature has been obtained by deriving spectroscopic redshifts for both components, lens and source, from observations at the 10.4\u00a0m Gran Telescopio CANARIAS (GTC) with the spectrograph OSIRIS. The lens, a massive early-type galaxy, has a redshift of <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.581, while the source is a starburst galaxy with redshift of <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.165. The total enclosed mass that produces the lensing effect has been estimated to be <em>M</em><sub>tot</sub>\u00a0=\u00a0(1.86 \u00b1 0.23)\u2009\u00d7\u200910<sup>12</sup>\u2009M<sub>\u2299</sub>.</p></section>                        <div class=\"article-metadata-panel clearfix\"></div>\r\n<div class=\"kwd-group\"><a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;gravitational lensing: strong&quot;\">gravitational lensing: strong</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;galaxies: distances and redshifts&quot;\">galaxies: distances and redshifts</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;galaxies: elliptical and lenticular, cD&quot;\">galaxies: elliptical and lenticular, cD</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;galaxies: evolution&quot;\">galaxies: evolution</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;galaxies: starburst&quot;\">galaxies: starburst</a></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=45586461 id=\"45586461\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec1>1 INTRODUCTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Strongly lensed galaxies are very important in the study of galaxy formation and evolution because they permit derivation of important physical parameters such as the total mass of the lensing object, without any assumption on the dynamics. Cases in which the Einstein ring (ER) is almost complete and the central lensing galaxy isolated are rare; these permit constraining with great accuracy the enclosed mass within the projected Einstein radius \u0398<sub>E</sub> (Kochanek, Keeton &amp; McLeod <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2001</a>). Miralda-Escud\u00e9 &amp; Leh\u00e1r (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1992</a>) predicted several 10<sup>6</sup> optical ER to be detectable over the whole sky, down to a magnitude limit of <em>B</em>\u00a0=\u00a026 and a lower limit for the enclosed mass of <em>M</em>\u00a0\u223c 5\u2009\u00d7\u200910<sup>11</sup>\u2009M<sub>\u2299</sub>. This notwithstanding, despite extensive surveys (see for example Bolton et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>; Stark et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>) only a few tens of complete or nearly complete optical ERs have been identified so far, and among these objects, only a few show a close similarity, in morphology and elongation of the ring, to the one we discuss in this present work.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The first ER to be discovered is the radio source MG1131+0456 (Hewitt et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib10\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib10\" data-open=\"bib10\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1988</a>). Warren et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1996</a>) report the discovery of a partial ER (\u223c170\u00b0) with \u0398<sub>E</sub>\u00a0\u223c 1.35\u2009arcsec; the background O<span class=\"small-caps\">\u00a0ii</span> emitting galaxy at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a03.595 is lensed by an elliptical massive galaxy at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.485. This is the first known case in the literature of an ER discovered at optical wavelengths. Cabanac et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2005</a>) discovered an almost complete ER (\u223c260\u00b0) with \u0398<sub>E</sub>\u00a0\u223c 1.48\u2009arcsec produced by a massive and isolated elliptical galaxy at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.986. The source galaxy is a starburst at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a03.773. Then, a similar ER to the one we report in this Letter, in morphology, but not in the physics of the source galaxy, a BX galaxy, is the so called Cosmic Horseshoe (Belokurov et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib2\" data-open=\"bib2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>); the ring extension is similar to the one we report here, (\u223c300\u00b0), but the Einstein radius is double, \u0398<sub>E</sub>\u00a0\u223c 5\u2009arcsec; the lensing galaxy has a huge mass of\u00a0\u223c<em>M</em>\u00a0=\u00a05.4\u2009\u00d7 10<sup>12</sup>\u2009M<sub>\u2299</sub>. Other partial ER discovered recently are: the \u2018Cosmic Eye\u2019 (Smail et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib21\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib21\" data-open=\"bib21\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>), the \u20188 o'clock arc\u2019 (Allam et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>) and the \u2018Clone\u2019 (Lin et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib15\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib15\" data-open=\"bib15\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Here, we report the discovery of IAC J010127-334319, an optical, almost complete ER, that we refer to as the \u2018Canarias Einstein Ring\u2019, noticed as a peculiar object in DECam images. No previous reference to the object has been found in the literature. Subsequently, we observed it with OSIRIS@GTC for a spectroscopic confirmation of its nature. In this Letter, we provide the first physical parameters of this system. In the following discussion, we assume that a flat cosmology with \u03a9<sub>m</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.3, \u03a9<sub>\u039b</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.7 and <em>H</em><sub>0</sub>\u00a0=\u00a070\u2009km\u2009s<sup>\u22121</sup>\u2009Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup>.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=45586467 id=\"45586467\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2>2 DISCOVERY</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The serendipitous discovery of IAC J010127-334319 was made, while performing photometry on stacked images, in <em>g</em> and <em>r</em> filters, taken with DECam (Flaugher et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib9\" data-open=\"bib9\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) at the Blanco 4\u00a0m telescope at the Cerro Tololo Inter-American Observatory (CTIO), reduced with the NOAO Community Pipeline (Valdes et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>) and obtained from the NOAO Science Archive (Seaman et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>). The total exposure time is 7680\u00a0s in the <em>g</em> filter and 5700\u00a0s in the <em>r</em> filter. Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a> shows the resulting colour composite image: it is evident that two components with different colours are present. In particular, the central one (the lens) appears redder than the second component (the lensed image of the source), which in turn appears as elongated all around the first. The ring is almost perfectly circular with an apparent radius of 8\u2009px which translates to 2.16\u2009arcsec. Three peaks, A, B and C, are clearly visible (bottom-right panel of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>); they are located respectively at \u2212150\u00b0, 14\u00b0 and 83\u00b0 from North counterclockwise. In Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>, all the derived parameters for the object are listed. From the DECam photometry, we estimated an apparent magnitude for the lens in both <em>g</em> and <em>r</em> bands of <em>g</em>\u00a0=\u00a023.61 and <em>r</em>\u00a0=\u00a021.40. The colour (<em>g</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>r</em>)\u00a0&gt;\u00a02 indicates that this galaxy is probably a luminous red galaxy (Eisenstein et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib8\" data-open=\"bib8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2001</a>). All the details about the photometric calibration will be given in a forthcoming paper (Bettinelli et\u00a0al., in preparation).</p>                        <a id=\"45586469\" scrollto-destination=\"45586469\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig1\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 1.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img view of 2.5\u2009arcmin\u00a0\u00d7\u00a02.5\u2009arcmin centred on the object (on the left), North is up, while East points left; a zoom of the object with overplotted the best-fitting circle, the slit position and width are also plotted as green lines (right upper panel); counts from photometry along the best-fitting circle of the ring (lower right panel): the measured sky value is indicated by the red solid line, and the 1\u03c3 value is indicated by the red dashed one.</p></div></div>                        <a id=\"45586470\" scrollto-destination=\"45586470\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/45586470\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=45586471 id=\"45586471\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3>3 FOLLOW-UP SPECTROSCOPY</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">In order to confirm the lensing nature of this system, we performed a spectroscopic follow-up at the 10.4\u00a0m Gran Telescopio CANARIAS (GTC) on Roque de los Muchachos Observatory (La Palma, Spain) using the Optical System for Imaging and low-Intermediate-Resolution Integrated Spectroscopy (OSIRIS) spectrograph (Cepa <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib6\" data-open=\"bib6\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1998</a>). OSIRIS has a mosaic of two E2V CCD42-82 (2048\u00a0\u00d7\u00a04096\u2009px). All the obtained spectra were registered on the second detector, which is the default for long-slit spectroscopy. We used a binning of 2\u00a0\u00d7\u00a02 providing a pixel size of 0.254\u2009arcsec\u2009px<sup>\u22121</sup>, and the grism R300B, which provides a spectral coverage of 4000\u20139000\u00a0\u00c5 and a nominal dispersion of 4.96\u00a0\u00c5 px<sup>\u22121</sup>. The slit width was 0.6\u2009arcsec. Long-slit spectral observations were performed on 2015 December 2 in good seeing conditions of\u00a0\u223c0.8\u2009arcsec. The slit was placed along the N\u2013S direction, in order to minimize the effects of atmospheric differential refraction at culmination. The total exposure time was 3600\u00a0s divided into six exposures of 600\u00a0s each. In each of the six exposures, the two components, ring and lensing galaxy, have been detected and in particular their spectra were not overlapping. The position of the slit was such that the spectra obtained for the ring refers to peak B.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">For the pre-reduction, we have used the OSIRIS Offline Pipeline Software (<span class=\"small-caps\">oops</span>); sky subtraction and flux calibration were performed using <span class=\"small-caps\">iraf</span>.<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn1\" data-open=\"fn1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\"><sup>1</sup></a> We performed wavelength calibration using standard HgAr+Ne+Xe arc lamps; the resulting error on wavelength determination has been measured to be consistent with the above spectral resolution. We corrected the extracted spectra for instrumental response using observations of the spectrophotometric standard star GD140, a white dwarf, obtained the same night. The fluxes of this standard star are available in Massey et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib16\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib16\" data-open=\"bib16\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1988</a>).</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=45586474 id=\"45586474\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4>4 ANALYSIS AND DISCUSSION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">In order to derive the redshifts for the two components, we noted the strong emission line in the source spectrum and the 4000\u00a0\u00c5 Balmer discontinuity in the lens spectrum. This led us to choose template models for a starburst galaxy and an early-type galaxy, respectively, as specified below. Following line identification, we determined redshifts.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=45586476 id=\"45586476\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4-1>4.1 Lens</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Using the template spectra by Kinney et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1996</a>) results that the spectrum of the lens galaxy fits well the spectrum of a S0 galaxy (see Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>), a typical early-type galaxy characterized by a large increase in flux from the UV part of the spectrum to the optical. The 4000 \u00c5 Balmer discontinuity at\u00a0\u223c6330 \u00c5 is noticeable. The redshift of the lens galaxy is <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.581 \u00b1 0.001, and it has been determined from the measurements of: H\u03b7\u2009\u03bb3835.4, Ca K \u03bb3933.7, Ca H \u03bb3968.5, H\u03b4\u2009\u03bb4141.8, <em>G</em>-band \u03bb4307.7, Mg-b2 \u03bb5172.7, Mg-b1 \u03bb5183.6 (marked red features from left to right in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> middle panel).</p>                        <a id=\"45586478\" scrollto-destination=\"45586478\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig2\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 2.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnrasl/461/1/10.1093_mnrasl_slw097/2/m_slw097fig2.jpeg?Expires=1611467003&amp;Signature=dQ95PdNHSlylwjsDmP7ZBhQ7jP0QfJxvpjFLExWcWgnG1khTu6mKzPQTZ5y6eSBQxCblbQTYMHHd-MIBYMzZWKZLdC-AB3J2wxKJFIdvqekfaw18bjrfNTsPdmbZ6u6SlUrmf4gcS26pNOTbbiMZOKtaJIr3poMZGOVzvknriiNfQ8URtfs6AGnKlX6RmYJwpQ7s08qNyLXoyanpkUt7EDb98-2UIXdk13R4oSyO8juC19a6xB6MKUQjKGodSaKA4rXRIilZF02XlcotIOoMxJf2hthXSPWY9qdJJ-WlHswdjIKOcUd9MKGFRS1IJTNOpLF8Sv8fZuBbt7I8U0nT1Q__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Top panel: source galaxy spectrum (in blue) with overplotted a starburst template spectrum by Calzetti, Kinney &amp; Storchi-Bergmann (1994). Bottom panel: measured wavelength displacement between observed and laboratory line position for the selected features (see text for details).</p></div></div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=45586479 id=\"45586479\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4-2>4.2 Source</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">For the source galaxy, we used the template spectra by Calzetti et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1994</a>), and we found that the spectrum best fitting our observed spectrum corresponds to a starburst galaxy in the case of clumpy scattering slab, where it is assumed that clumped dust is located close to the source of radiation. In such circumstances, Calzetti et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1994</a>) show that scattering into the line of sight dominates over absorption by the dust, providing a significant positive contribution to the emerging radiation. This template spectrum fits well the strong O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> \u03bb3727 emission line. We also identified the following lines: Fe\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> \u03bb2344.0, Fe\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> \u03bb2600.0, H\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">i</span>\u00a011 \u03bb3770.6, O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> \u03bb3727.3, H\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">i</span>\u00a010 \u03bb3797.9 (marked blue features from left to right in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> upper panel). According to these features, we derived for the source galaxy a redshift of <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.165 \u00b1 0.001. We note that the selected slit position enable us to extract only the portion of the spectrum corresponding to peak B (see Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>); this notwithstanding, the O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> emission coming from the opposite side of the ring can be easily noted in our spectra.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=45586481 id=\"45586481\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4-3>4.3 Enclosed mass derivation</h3>\r\n<div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">The strong circular symmetry, of our object (see Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>), suggests that it can be approximated to the case of a circularly symmetric lens, with source and lens in the line of sight. Under these assumptions, for an arbitrary mass profile M(\u0398) (i.e. without assuming any particular model for the potential), we can apply the following relation (Narayan &amp; Bartelmann <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib19\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib19\" data-open=\"bib19\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1996</a>) and solve it for the mass. <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ1\" content-id=\"equ1\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{equation}\r\n\\Theta ^{2}_{\\rm E}\\, =\\, \\frac{4{\\rm G}}{\\rm c^{2}}\\, {\\rm M}(\\Theta )\\, \\frac{\\mathrm{d}_{\\rm LS}}{\\mathrm{d}_{\\rm L}d_{\\rm S}}\r\n\\end{equation} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(1)</span></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Here, \u0398<sub>E</sub> is the Einstein radius in radians; M(\u0398) is the mass enclosed within the Einstein radius; <em>d</em><sub>LS</sub>, <em>d</em><sub>L</sub>, <em>d</em><sub>S</sub> are the angular diameter distances, respectively, of source-lens, lens-observer and source-observer. These last quantities are related to the relative comoving distances and, in general, this relation depends on the assumed curvature of the Universe (Hogg <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1999</a>). In our case, \u03a9<sub>K</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00 has been assumed, and the resulting angular diameter distances are <em>d</em><sub>L</sub>\u00a0=\u00a0951\u2009h<sup>\u22121</sup> Mpc, <em>d</em><sub>S</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01192\u2009h<sup>\u22121</sup> Mpc and <em>d</em><sub>LS</sub>\u00a0=\u00a0498\u2009h<sup>\u22121</sup> Mpc. We calculated a total mass <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\rm M_{tot}=(1.86 \\pm 0.23) \\,\\times 10^{12}\\, {\\rm M_{{\\odot }}}}$|</span> where the error on the mass (12\u2009per\u2009cent) is overwhelmingly due to the measurement error in the determination of the Einstein radius, which we have estimated to be 0.5\u2009px which corresponds to 0.135\u2009arcsec. The error on the redshift derives from the error estimated on the wavelength calibration, which is\u00a0\u223c5\u00a0\u00c5. This value is consistent with the spectral resolution (4.96\u00a0\u00c5 px<sup>\u22121</sup>) of the grating R300B that we used.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Under the assumption of a singular isothermal sphere (SIS), it is possible to give an estimate of the magnification of the ring: \u03bc\u00a0=\u00a04\u0398<sub>E</sub>/\u03b4\u0398<sub>s</sub>, where \u03b4\u0398<sub>s</sub> is the source size. From Nagy et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>), the average size of a starburst galaxy in our redshift range is\u00a0\u223c2 Kpc, which corresponds to 0.24\u2009arcsec. The derived magnification is\u00a0\u223c36.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We determined also the mass-to-light ratio of the lens in the g band; a <em>K</em>-correction of 2.1 has been derived for the lens using the NED calculator (Chilingarian &amp; Zolotukhin <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>). The resulting ratio is M<sub>tot</sub>/L\u00a0\u223c 58\u2009M<sub>\u2299</sub>/L<sub>\u2299</sub>.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The former mass estimate can be improved by applying to the system a singular isothermal ellipsoid (SIE) model using the <span class=\"small-caps\">gravlens/lensmodel</span> software (Keeton <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2001</a>). This software allows to fit a SIE model using only the image positions and fluxes. The obtained best-fitting model is plotted in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>. The solutions have been derived for point-like sources; the ring shape is due to the fact that the source should actually be more extended with respect to the caustics than is shown here. The best fit ellipticity is 0.2 calculated as 1\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>q</em>, where <em>q</em> is the axis ratio; the associated position angle is \u221257\u00b0, angle measured from North to East. The best-fitting \u03c7<sup>2</sup> value is 6.12, calculated setting to 0 the weights relative to image fluxes. The derived Einstein radius is \u0398<sub>E</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.38\u2009arcsec, which translates in an enclosed mass of\u00a0\u223c2.26\u2009\u00d7\u200910<sup>12</sup>\u2009M<sub>\u2299</sub>, hence, in excellent agreement with our previous estimate.</p>                        <a id=\"45586487\" scrollto-destination=\"45586487\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig3\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 3.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnrasl/461/1/10.1093_mnrasl_slw097/2/m_slw097fig3.jpeg?Expires=1611467003&amp;Signature=aX8sMFyrc965mhtX4T7epk~b2N01eLX59zQHg69zxMYc7WAhExEZBIso5JO5yP4PCbOlDrF6Nze7U4jhZVrKgnrvTgQt2ydIFxRX9Ha20I4vb9lDuGR1VNeyhrz-wDvaFPcz0rBGYJYy0ruFkt~ia463J5m3SdDc04u8ySoyfE2cKuQ1QlCJoC15PGHukZ32JZevD9bWonAKAdxClYaRWimKtyPVZJfdjBQbMSnCkACptlUHCXtC4KOh3oCgqgzxoLKGzqp1JtVR7~5rDnSQ3OCVQOVH~tBOOU-27cGjC0Ftj42pLTaoyQ4sFufWXgq6IKC-I-77iwY9Z~gOL0zBww__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Best-fitting SIE model obtained with the gravlens/lensmodel software. On the left (image plane): the source images positions are plotted as blue triangles, the fitted position recovered by the software as blue squares, the red central dot represents the position of the lensing galaxy and the red curve is the critical curve. On the right (source plane): the blue square represents the calculated position of the source; the caustics are shown in red.</p></div></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=45586488 id=\"45586488\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5>5 CONCLUSIONS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We report the discovery of an almost complete (\u223c300\u00b0) circular optical ER in the constellation of Sculptor. The gravitational lens is a massive luminous red galaxy at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.581. The source galaxy is a starburst at redshift <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.165; its spectrum is dominated by a strong O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> emission line. Using these redshift determinations and the Einstein radius \u0398<sub>E</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.16\u2009arcsec, we calculated the total enclosed mass that produced the lensing effect: <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\rm M_{tot}=(1.86 \\pm 0.23) \\times 10^{12}\\, {\\rm M_{{\\odot }}}}$|\u2060</span>.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">All the parameters, we determined for IAC J010127-334319, are listed in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The authors thank the anonymous referee for the constructive comments that significantly improved the manuscript. The authors are grateful to all the GTC staff and in particular to Dr A. Cabrera-Lavers for his support in refining the spectroscopical observations during the Phase-2. The authors also thank Dr J. Falc\u00f3n-Barroso for the helpful discussion.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">This Letter is based on observations made with the GTC telescope, in the Spanish Observatorio del Roque de los Muchachos of the Instituto de Astrof\u00edsica de Canarias, under Director's Discretionary Time.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">This project used data obtained with theDECam, which was constructed by the Dark Energy Survey (DES) collaboration. Funding for the DES Projects has been provided by the DOE and NSF (USA), MISE (Spain), STFC (UK), HEFCE (UK), NCSA (UIUC), KICP (U. Chicago), CCAPP (Ohio State), MIFPA (Texas A&amp;M), CNPQ, FAPERJ, FINEP (Brazil), MINECO (Spain), DFG (Germany) and the collaborating institutions in the Dark Energy Survey, which are Argonne Lab, UC Santa Cruz, University of Cambridge, CIEMAT-Madrid, University of Chicago, University College London, DES-Brazil Consortium, University of Edinburgh, ETH Z\u00fcrich, Fermilab, University of Illinois, ICE (IEEC-CSIC), IFAE Barcelona, Lawrence Berkeley Lab, LMU M\u00fcnchen and the associated Excellence Cluster Universe, University of Michigan, NOAO, University of Nottingham, Ohio State University, University of Pennsylvania, University of Portsmouth, SLAC National Lab, Stanford University, University of Sussex and Texas A&amp;M University.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">MB, MS, AA, SLH, SC and GP acknowledge support from the Spanish Ministry of Economy and Competitiveness (MINECO) under grant AYA2013-42781.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">This research has made use of the NASA/IPAC Extragalactic Database (NED), which is operated by the Jet Propulsion Laboratory, California Institute of Technology, under contract with the National Aeronautics and Space Administration.</p><div "https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2016MNRAS.461L..67B", "Tables status": "Complete", "Inspection status": "Incomplete", "Paper Overview": {"abstract": "We report the discovery of an optical Einstein ring in the Sculptor constellation, IAC J010127-334319, in the vicinity of the Sculptor dwarf spheroidal galaxy. It is an almost complete ring (\u223c300\u00b0) with a diameter of \u223c4.5 arcsec. The discovery was made serendipitously from inspecting Dark Energy Camera (DECam) archive imaging data. Confirmation of the object nature has been obtained by deriving spectroscopic redshifts for both components, lens and source, from observations at the 10.4 m Gran Telescopio CANARIAS (GTC) with the spectrograph OSIRIS. The lens, a massive early-type galaxy, has a redshift of z = 0.581, while the source is a starburst galaxy with redshift of z = 1.165. The total enclosed mass that produces the lensing effect has been estimated to be M<SUB>tot</SUB> = (1.86 \u00b1 0.23) \u00d7 10<SUP>12</SUP> M<SUB>\u2609</SUB>.", "start_page": "L67", "authors": ["Bettinelli, M.", "Simioni, M.", "Aparicio, A.", "Hidalgo, S.
